<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Defense.gov_photo_essay_100421-G-0000L-003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Defense.gov_photo_essay_100421-G-0000L-003.jpg/220px-Defense.gov_photo_essay_100421-G-0000L-003.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Defense.gov_photo_essay_100421-G-0000L-003.jpg/330px-Defense.gov_photo_essay_100421-G-0000L-003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Defense.gov_photo_essay_100421-G-0000L-003.jpg/440px-Defense.gov_photo_essay_100421-G-0000L-003.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Defense.gov_photo_essay_100421-G-0000L-003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 2010 <a href="/wiki/Deepwater_Horizon_oil_spill" title="Deepwater Horizon oil spill">Deepwater Horizon oil spill</a> discharges 4.9 million barrels</div></div></div>
<p><b>Fossil fuel phase out</b> refers to the discontinuation of the use of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil fuels">fossil fuels</a>, through the decommissioning of operating <a href="/wiki/Fossil-fuel_power_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil-fuel power station">fossil fuel-fired power plants</a>, the prevention of the construction of new ones, and the use of <a href="/wiki/Alternative_energy" title="Alternative energy">alternative energy</a> to replace the role of fossil fuels.
</p><p>The purpose of fossil fuel phase-out is to reduce the negative <a href="/wiki/Externalities" class="mw-redirect" title="Externalities">externalities</a> that use of fossil fuels cause. Negative externalities refer to the costs a certain activity has over people who did not choose to incur in them. A direct negative externality from fossil fuels' use is <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a>, and an indirect negative externality are <a href="/wiki/Mining_accidents" class="mw-redirect" title="Mining accidents">mining accidents</a>, that happen as a consequence of the extraction of fossil fuels. Fossil fuel burning contributes to <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, as it releases <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" class="mw-redirect" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">greenhouse gas emissions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fossil_fuels">Fossil fuels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Fossil fuels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coal">Coal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Coal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Top_5_Coal_Consumers.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Top_5_Coal_Consumers.png/220px-Top_5_Coal_Consumers.png" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Top_5_Coal_Consumers.png/330px-Top_5_Coal_Consumers.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Top_5_Coal_Consumers.png/440px-Top_5_Coal_Consumers.png 2x" data-file-width="2200" data-file-height="1700" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Top_5_Coal_Consumers.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coal consumption trends 1980–2012 in the top five coal-consuming countries (US EIA)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Castle_Gate_Power_Plant,_Utah_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Castle_Gate_Power_Plant%2C_Utah_2007.jpg/220px-Castle_Gate_Power_Plant%2C_Utah_2007.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Castle_Gate_Power_Plant%2C_Utah_2007.jpg/330px-Castle_Gate_Power_Plant%2C_Utah_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Castle_Gate_Power_Plant%2C_Utah_2007.jpg/440px-Castle_Gate_Power_Plant%2C_Utah_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2293" data-file-height="1439" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Castle_Gate_Power_Plant,_Utah_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coal-fired power plants provided 30% of consumed electricity in the United States in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> This is the <a href="/wiki/Carbon_Power_Plant" title="Carbon Power Plant">Castle Gate Plant</a> near <a href="/wiki/Helper,_Utah" title="Helper, Utah">Helper, Utah</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Coal is one of the largest sources of energy, supplying 28.6% percent of the world's primary energy in 2014 (equivalent to 3,917 <a href="/wiki/Tonne_of_oil_equivalent" title="Tonne of oil equivalent">Mtoe</a>) according to the <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Coal combustion accounted for 14,863 Mt of CO<sub>2</sub> emissions in 2014, which is equivalent to a 45.9% of fossil fuel emissions from combustion (excluding non-energy emissions).<sup id="cite_ref-:0_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To decrease carbon emissions and thus possibly stop extreme climate change, some have called for coal to be phased out.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Climatologist James E. Hansen said "We need a moratorium on coal now...with phase-out of existing plants over the next two decades."<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> According to a study published in <a href="/wiki/Science_(journal)" title="Science (journal)">Science</a> in 2017, coal has to be phased-out globally by about 2030, if the agreed 2&#160;°C target is taken seriously.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some nations have decreased their coal consumption thus far in the 21st century, the greatest reductions being in the United States (coal consumption reduced by 176 million metric tons per year over the period 2000-2012), Canada (reduced by 21 million tons per year) and Spain (20 million tons per year). Other nations have increased their coal consumption in the same period, led by China (increased 2,263 million metric tons per year in the period 2000-2012), India (increased 367 million tons per year), and South Korea (59 million tons per year). Worldwide, coal consumption increased 60% during the period 2000-2012.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> As of 2012, 1200 new coal power plants were reportedly being planned worldwide, most of them in China and India.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In the 2011-2013 period, the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> group of Western European countries has increased the use of coal, attributed largely to the low cost of coal and the high price of imported natural gas in Western Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
However, coal consumption has peaked in China in 2013 or 2014, depending on the data used and fell in 2015 by 3.6%, even though there was a growth of GDP of 6.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Worldwide coal consumption peaked in 2014 and declined in 2015 and 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/Scientific_American" title="Scientific American">Scientific American</a>, the average coal plant emits more than 100 times as much radiation per year than does a comparatively sized nuclear power plant, in the form of fly ash.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some like the "coal advisory board" of the IEA believe that coal should not be phased out, considering that longer-term global economic growth cannot be achieved without adequate and affordable energy supplies, which will require continuing significant contributions from fossil fuels including coal. In this viewpoint, <a href="/wiki/Clean_coal_technology" title="Clean coal technology">clean coal technology</a> could reduce <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> emissions compatible with a low-emissions future.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Some environmentalists and climatologists support a phase-out and criticise clean coal as not a solution to <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Entrepreneurs promote improved regulations and modernised technology.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Sometimes coal is replaced by natural gas, which has lower carbon emissions and produces less pollutants. However natural gas is also a fossil fuel, so a switch from coal to natural gas does not contribute to a fossil fuel phase-out.
</p><p>As of October 2018, 28 national governments, 19 sub-national governments and 28 organisations<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> had become members of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Powering_Past_Coal_Alliance&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Powering Past Coal Alliance (page does not exist)">Powering Past Coal Alliance</a>, each making a declaration to advance the transition away from unabated coal power generation.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil">Oil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Oil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small><i>(September 2018)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Oil is refined into <a href="/wiki/Fuel_oil" title="Fuel oil">fuel oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diesel_fuel" title="Diesel fuel">diesel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">gasoline</a>. The refined products are primarily for transportation by conventional cars, trucks, trains, planes and ships.  Popular alternatives are <a href="/wiki/Human-powered_transport" title="Human-powered transport">Human-powered transport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">public transport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicles" class="mw-redirect" title="Electric vehicles">electric vehicles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Biofuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Biofuels">biofuels</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_gas">Natural gas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Natural gas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">Natural gas</a></div>
<p>Although natural gas has about half the carbon intensity of coal it is also the single largest source of <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_methane" title="Atmospheric methane">atmospheric methane</a> in the United States. It is seen by many as a temporary "bridge fuel" to replace coal, but in turn to be replaced by renewable sources. However this "bridge fuel" is likely to  significantly extend the use of fossil fuel as the average plant life is 35 years.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Gas consumption has tripled since 1971, and by 2015 it was generating half as much electricity as coal.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Since the consumption of gas is expected to grow an additional 10% by 2040, the phase out is likely to be many years in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Basis">Basis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Basis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The basis of phasing-out fossil fuels consists mainly of the projected lower cost of renewable sources of energy,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> but the avoidance of risks in health and <a href="/wiki/Mitigation_of_global_warming" class="mw-redirect" title="Mitigation of global warming">mitigation of global warming</a> are also important considerations.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Using computer modeling he developed over 20 years, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Z._Jacobson" title="Mark Z. Jacobson">Mark Z. Jacobson</a> has found that <a href="/wiki/Carbon" title="Carbon">carbonaceous</a> fuel <a href="/wiki/Particulate_matter" class="mw-redirect" title="Particulate matter">soot emissions</a> (which lead to respiratory illness, heart disease, and asthma) have resulted in 1.5 million premature deaths each year, mostly in the developing world where the non-fossil fuels wood and animal dung are used for cooking. Jacobson has also said that soot from diesel engines, coal-fired power plants, and burning wood is a "bigger cause of global warming than previously thought, and is the major cause of the rapid melting of the Arctic's sea ice".<sup id="cite_ref-dp_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dp-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011, new evidence has emerged that there are considerable risks associated with traditional energy sources, and that major changes to the mix of energy technologies are needed:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Several mining tragedies globally have underscored the human toll of the coal supply chain. New EPA initiatives targeting air toxics, coal ash, and effluent releases highlight the environmental impacts of coal and the cost of addressing them with control technologies. The use of fracking in natural gas exploration is coming under scrutiny, with evidence of groundwater contamination and greenhouse gas emissions. Concerns are increasing about the vast amounts of water used at coal-fired plants, particularly in regions of the country facing water shortages.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_warming_mitigation">Global warming mitigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Global warming mitigation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">Global warming</a></div><p>In 2008, <a href="/wiki/James_E._Hansen" class="mw-redirect" title="James E. Hansen">James Hansen</a> and nine other scientists published a journal article titled "Target atmospheric CO<sub>2</sub>: Where should humanity aim?" which calls for a complete phase-out of coal power by 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-hansen-etal-2008_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hansen-etal-2008-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>More recently, Hansen has stated that continued <a href="/wiki/Opposition_to_nuclear_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Opposition to nuclear power">opposition to nuclear power</a> threatens humanity's ability to avoid dangerous climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The letter, co-authored with other climate change experts declared "If we stay on the current path," he said, "those are the consequences we'll be leaving to our children. The best candidate to avoid that is nuclear power. It's ready now. We need to take advantage of it." and "Continued opposition to nuclear power threatens humanity's ability to avoid dangerous climate change."
</p><p>Also in 2008, Pushker Kharecha and James Hansen published a peer-reviewed scientific study analyzing the effect of a coal phase-out on atmospheric <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> (CO<sub>2</sub>) levels.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Their baseline mitigation scenario was a phaseout of global coal emissions by 2050. The authors describe the scenario as follows:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The second scenario, labeled Coal Phase-out, is meant to approximate a situation in which developed countries freeze their CO<sub>2</sub> emissions from coal by 2012 and a decade later developing countries similarly halt increases in coal emissions.  Between 2025 and 2050 it is assumed that both developed and developing countries will linearly phase out emissions of CO<sub>2</sub> from coal usage.  Thus in Coal Phase-out we have global CO<sub>2</sub> emissions from coal increasing 2% per year until 2012, 1% per year growth of coal emissions between 2013 and 2022, flat coal emissions for 2023–2025, and finally a linear decrease to zero CO<sub>2</sub> emissions from coal in 2050.  These rates refer to emissions to the atmosphere and do not constrain consumption of coal, provided the CO<sub>2</sub> is captured and sequestered. Oil and gas emissions are assumed to be the same as in the BAU [business as usual] scenario.
</p></blockquote>
<p>Kharecha and Hansen also consider three other mitigation scenarios, all with the same coal phase-out schedule but each making different assumptions about the size of oil and gas reserves and the speed at which they are depleted. Under the Business as Usual scenario, atmospheric CO<sub>2</sub> peaks at 563 parts per million (ppm) in the year 2100. Under the four coal phase-out scenarios, atmospheric CO<sub>2</sub> peaks at 422-446 ppm between 2045 and 2060 and declines thereafter. The key implications of the study are as follows: a phase-out of coal emissions is the most important remedy for mitigating human-induced global warming; actions should be taken toward limiting or stretching out the use of conventional oil and gas; and strict emissions-based constraints are needed for future use of unconventional fossil fuels such as <a href="/wiki/Methane_hydrates" class="mw-redirect" title="Methane hydrates">methane hydrates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tar_sands" class="mw-redirect" title="Tar sands">tar sands</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Others">Others</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Others">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The impulse of renewable energy can create jobs through the construction of new power plants and the manufacturing of the equipment that they need, as could be seen in the case of Germany and the wind power industry.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinrichs_285–305_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinrichs_285–305-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Studies_about_fossil_fuel_phase-out">Studies about fossil fuel phase-out</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Studies about fossil fuel phase-out">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a> and EREC's Energy (R)evolution scenario,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> the world would eliminate all fossil fuel use by 2090.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2015 <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_Action_Network" title="Climate Action Network">Climate Action Network Europe</a> released a report highlighting the need for an active phase-out of coal-fired generation across Europe.  Their analysis derived from a database of 280 coal plants and included emissions data from official EU registries.<sup id="cite_ref-jones-and-gutmann-2015_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jones-and-gutmann-2015-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A September 2016 report by Oil Change International concludes that the carbon emissions embedded in the coal, oil, and gas in currently working mines and fields, assuming that these run to the end of their working lifetimes, will take the world to just beyond the 2&#8239;°C limit contained in the 2015 <a href="/wiki/Paris_Agreement" title="Paris Agreement">Paris Agreement</a> and even further from the 1.5&#8239;°C goal.<sup id="cite_ref-mathiesen-2016_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mathiesen-2016-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-turnbull-2016_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-turnbull-2016-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-muttitt-2016_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-muttitt-2016-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>  The report observes that "one of the most powerful climate policy levers is also the simplest: stop digging for more fossil fuels".<sup id="cite_ref-muttitt-2016_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-muttitt-2016-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>5</span></sup>
</p><p>In October 2016, the <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Development_Institute" title="Overseas Development Institute">Overseas Development Institute</a> (ODI) and 11 other <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">NGOs</a> released a report on the impact of building new coal-fired power plants in countries where a significant proportion of the population lacks access to electricity.  The report concludes that, on the whole, building coal-fired power plants does little to help the poor and may make them poorer.  Moreover, wind and solar generation are beginning to challenge coal on cost.<sup id="cite_ref-nuccitelli-2016_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nuccitelli-2016-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-granoff-etal-2016-webpage_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-granoff-etal-2016-webpage-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-granoff-etal-2016-report_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-granoff-etal-2016-report-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2018 study in Nature Energy suggests that 10 countries in Europe could completely phase out coal-fired electricity generation with their current infrastructure, whilst the US and Russia could phase out at least 30%.<sup id="cite_ref-wilson-and-staffell-2018_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wilson-and-staffell-2018-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Challenges_of_fossil_fuel_phase-out">Challenges of fossil fuel phase-out</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Challenges of fossil fuel phase-out">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The phase-out of fossil fuels involves many challenges, and one of them is the reliance that currently the world has on them. In 2014, fossil fuels provided 81.1% of the <a href="/wiki/Primary_energy_consumption" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary energy consumption">primary energy consumption</a> of the world, with approximately 11,109 Mtoe. This number is composed by 4,287 Mtoe of oil consumption; 3,918 Mtoe of coal consumption, and 2,904 Mtoe of natural gas consumption .<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Fossil fuel phase-out can lead to an increment in electricity prices, because of the new investments needed to replace their share in the electricity mix with alternative energy sources.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Another cause to increasing electricity price comes from the need to import the electricity that can't be generated nationally.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another impact of a phase-out of fossil fuels is in the employment. In the case of employments in the fossil fuel industry, a phase-out is logically undesired, therefore, people in the industry will usually oppose any measures that put their industries under scrutiny.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinrichs_285–305_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinrichs_285–305-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Endre Tvinnereim and Elisabeth Ivarsflaten studied the relationship between employment in the fossil fuel industry with the support to climate change policies. They proposed that one opportunity for displaced drilling employments in the fossil fuel industry could be in the geothermal energy industry. This was suggested as a result of their conclusion: people and companies in the fossil fuel industry will likely oppose measures that endanger their employments, unless they have other stronger alternatives.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> This can be extrapolated to political interests, that can push against the phase-out of fossil fuels initiative. One example is how the vote of U.S. Congress members is related to the preeminence of fossil fuel industries in their respective states.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislation_and_initiatives_to_phase_out_coal">Legislation and initiatives to phase out coal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Legislation and initiatives to phase out coal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_economies">Major economies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Major economies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 8 June 2015, several newspapers ran an article wrote that the leaders of the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_Seven" title="Group of Seven">Group of Seven</a> (or G7, consisting of <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>) agreed to phase-out fossil fuel use by 2100,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> as part of the efforts to keep global temperature increase under 2&#8239;°C. This was done as a prelude for the United Nations Climate Change Conference (a.k.a. <a href="/wiki/COP_21" class="mw-redirect" title="COP 21">COP 21</a>) hosted in Paris, on December of the same year.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Graph_RE_Australia_2010.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Graph_RE_Australia_2010.svg/220px-Graph_RE_Australia_2010.svg.png" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Graph_RE_Australia_2010.svg/330px-Graph_RE_Australia_2010.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Graph_RE_Australia_2010.svg/440px-Graph_RE_Australia_2010.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Graph_RE_Australia_2010.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Electricity generation from renewable sources in Australia in 2010</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Australian_Greens" title="Australian Greens">Australian Greens</a> party have proposed to phase out coal power stations. The NSW Greens proposed an immediate moratorium on coal-fired power stations and want to end all coal mining and <a href="/wiki/Coal_industry_subsidies" class="mw-redirect" title="Coal industry subsidies">coal industry subsidies</a>.  The Australian Greens and the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Labor_Party" title="Australian Labor Party">Australian Labor Party</a> also oppose nuclear power.  The Federal Government and Victorian State Government want to modify existing coal-fired power stations into clean coal power stations.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The Federal Labor government extended the <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Renewable_Energy_Target#Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Mandatory Renewable Energy Target">mandatory renewable energy targets</a>, an initiative to ensure that new sources of electricity are more likely to be from wind power, solar power and other sources of <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_in_Australia" title="Renewable energy in Australia">renewable energy in Australia</a>.  <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> is one of the largest consumers of coal per capita, and also the largest exporter. The proposals are strongly opposed by industry, unions<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> and the main Opposition Party in Parliament (now forming the party in government after the September 2013 election).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2005, Canada annually burned 60 million tons of coal, mainly for electrical power, increasing by 15 percent annually.
</p><p>In November 2016, Canada announced plans to phase-out coal-fired electricity generation by 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-the-guardian-2016_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-the-guardian-2016-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Beginning in 2005 <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> planned coal phase-out legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Ontario annually consumed 15 million tons of coal in large power plants to supplement nuclear power. <a href="/wiki/Nanticoke_Generating_Station" title="Nanticoke Generating Station">Nanticoke Generating Station</a> was a major source of air pollution, and Ontario suffered "smog days" during the summer.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
In 2007, Ontario's Liberal government committed to phasing out all coal generation in the province by 2014. Premier Dalton McGuinty said, "By 2030 there will be about 1,000 more new coal-fired generating stations built on this planet. There is only one place in the world that is phasing out coal-fired generation and we're doing that right here in Ontario."<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The Ontario Power Authority projects that in 2014, with no coal generation, the largest sources of electrical power in the province will be nuclear (57 percent), hydroelectricity (25 percent), and natural gas (11 percent).<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In April 2014 <a href="/wiki/Ontario_electricity_policy" title="Ontario electricity policy">Ontario Canada</a> was the first jurisdiction in North America to eliminate coal in electricity generation.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The final coal plant in Ontario, <a href="/wiki/Thunder_Bay_Generating_Station" title="Thunder Bay Generating Station">Thunder Bay Generating Station</a>, stopped burning coal in April 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are currently no plans to phase out coal burning power stations in the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a> on the national level.
</p><p>China’s exceedingly high energy demand has pushed the demand for relatively cheap coal-fired power. Each week, another 2GW of coal-fired power is put online in China.  Coal supplies about 80% of China's energy needs today, and that ratio is expected to continue, even as overall power usage grows rapidly. Serious air quality deterioration has resulted from the massive use of coal and many Chinese cities suffer severe smog events.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>As a consequence the region of Beijing has decided to phase out all its coal-fired power generation by the end of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (November 2016)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In 2009 China had 172GW of installed hydro capacity the largest in the world, producing 16% of China's electricity, the Eleventh Five-Year Plan has set a 300GW target for 2020. China built the world's largest power plant of any kind, the <a href="/wiki/Three_Gorges_Dam" title="Three Gorges Dam">Three Gorges Dam</a>.
</p><p>In addition to the huge investments in coal power, China has 32<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> reactors under construction, the highest number in the world.
</p><p>Analysis in 2016 shows that China's coal consumption appears to have peaked in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-carrington-2016_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carrington-2016-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-qi-etal-2016_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qi-etal-2016-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union">European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In July 2014, <a href="/wiki/Climate_Action_Network" title="Climate Action Network">CAN Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">WWF European Policy Office</a>, HEAL, <a href="/wiki/European_Environmental_Bureau" title="European Environmental Bureau">EEB</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate-Alliance_Germany" title="Climate-Alliance Germany">Climate-Alliance Germany</a> published a report calling for the decommissioning of the thirty most polluting coal-fired power plants in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-gutmann-etal-2014_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gutmann-etal-2014-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Denmark">Denmark</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Denmark">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>As part of their Climate policy Plan, Denmark stated that it will phase out oil for heating purposes and coal by 2030. Additionally, their goal is to supply a 100% of their electricity and heating needs with renewable energy five years later (i.e. 2035).<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Emmanuel_Macron_(2017-05-29,_cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Emmanuel_Macron_%282017-05-29%2C_cropped%29.jpg/220px-Emmanuel_Macron_%282017-05-29%2C_cropped%29.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Emmanuel_Macron_%282017-05-29%2C_cropped%29.jpg/330px-Emmanuel_Macron_%282017-05-29%2C_cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Emmanuel_Macron_%282017-05-29%2C_cropped%29.jpg/440px-Emmanuel_Macron_%282017-05-29%2C_cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1326" data-file-height="939" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Emmanuel_Macron_(2017-05-29,_cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>On 30 December 2017, <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Macron" title="Emmanuel Macron">Emmanuel Macron</a> signed a law planning the end of fossil-fuel extraction in French territories.</div></div></div>
<p>In December 2017, to fight against <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>, France adopted a law banning new <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuel</a> exploitation projects and closing current ones by 2040 in all of its territories. France thus became the first country to programme the end of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuel</a> exploitation.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ende_Gelaende_Einzug_Tagebau_Tag_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Ende_Gelaende_Einzug_Tagebau_Tag_1.jpg/220px-Ende_Gelaende_Einzug_Tagebau_Tag_1.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Ende_Gelaende_Einzug_Tagebau_Tag_1.jpg/330px-Ende_Gelaende_Einzug_Tagebau_Tag_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Ende_Gelaende_Einzug_Tagebau_Tag_1.jpg/440px-Ende_Gelaende_Einzug_Tagebau_Tag_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="530" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ende_Gelaende_Einzug_Tagebau_Tag_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>3,500-4,000 <a href="/wiki/Environmental_activist" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental activist">environmental activists</a> blocking a coal mine to <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">limit climate change</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ende_Gel%C3%A4nde_2016" title="Ende Gelände 2016">Ende Gelände 2016</a>).</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hard_coal" class="mw-redirect" title="Hard coal">Hard coal</a> mining has long been subsidized in Germany, reaching a peak of €6.7<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion in 1996 and dropping to €2.7<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion in 2005 due to falling output.  These subsidies represent a burden on public finances and imply a substantial <a href="/wiki/Opportunity_cost" title="Opportunity cost">opportunity cost</a>, diverting funds away from other, more beneficial public investments.<sup id="cite_ref-frondel-etal-2007_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frondel-etal-2007-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007 Germany announced plans to phase out hard coal-industry subsidies by 2018, a move which is expected to end hard coal mining in Germany. <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The text near this tag is dated. (January 2018)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> This exit is later than the EU-mandated end by 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Solar and wind are major sources of energy and renewable energy generation, around 15% as of December 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> and growing. Coal is still the largest source of power in Germany.
</p><p>In 2007 <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany" title="Chancellor of Germany">German Chancellor</a> <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> and her party agreed to legislation to phase out Germany's hard coal mining sector. That does not mean that they support phasing out coal in general. There were plans to build about 25 new plants in the coming years. Most German coal power plants were built in the 1960s, and have a low energy efficiency. Public sentiment against coal power plants is growing and the construction or planning of some plants has been stopped.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> A number are under construction and still being built. No concrete plan is in place to reduce coal-fired electricity generation. As of October 2015, the remaining coal plants still under planning include: Niederaussem, Profen, and Stade. The coal plants currently under construction include: Mannheim, Hamm D, Datteln, and Willhelmshaven. Between 2012 and 2015, six new plants went online. All of these plants are 600–1800 MW<sub>e</sub>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014 Germany's coal consumption dropped for the first time, having risen each year since the low during the 2009 recession.<sup id="cite_ref-bp-statistical-review-2015_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bp-statistical-review-2015-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2014 study finds that coal is not making a comeback in Germany, as is sometimes claimed.  Rather renewables have more than offset the nuclear facilities that have been shutdown as a result of Germany's <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_phase-out#Germany" title="Nuclear power phase-out">nuclear phase-out</a> (<i>Atomausstieg</i>).  Hard coal plants now face financial stringency as their operating hours are cut back by the market.  But in contrast, <a href="/wiki/Lignite" title="Lignite">lignite</a>-fired generation is in a safe position until the <span class="nowrap">mid-2020s</span> unless government policies change.  To phase-out coal, Germany should seek to strength the emissions trading system (<a href="/wiki/European_Union_Emission_Trading_Scheme" title="European Union Emission Trading Scheme">EU-ETS</a>), consider a carbon tax, promote <a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">energy efficiency</a>, and strengthen the use of natural gas as a bridge fuel.<sup id="cite_ref-jungjohann-and-morris-2014_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jungjohann-and-morris-2014-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016 the German government and affected <a href="/wiki/Lignite" title="Lignite">lignite</a> power plant operators <a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitteldeutsche_Braunkohlengesellschaft" class="extiw" title="de:Mitteldeutsche Braunkohlengesellschaft">Mibrag</a>, <a href="/wiki/RWE" title="RWE">RWE</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vattenfall" title="Vattenfall">Vattenfall</a> reached an understanding (<i>Verständigung</i>) on the transfer of lignite power plant units into security standby (<i>Überführung von Braunkohlekraftwerksblöcken in die Sicherheitsbereitschaft</i>).  As a result, eight lignite-fired power plants are to be mothballed and later closed, with the first plant scheduled to cease operation in October 2016 and the last in October 2019.  The affected operators will receive state compensation for foregone profits.  The <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> has declared government plans to use €1.6<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion of public financing for this purpose to be in line with EU <a href="/wiki/State_aid" class="mw-redirect" title="State aid">state aid</a> rules.<sup id="cite_ref-german-energy-blog-2016_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-german-energy-blog-2016-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2016 study finds that the phase-out of lignite in <a href="/wiki/Lusatia" title="Lusatia">Lusatia</a> (<i>Lausitz</i>) by 2030 can be financed by future owner <a href="/wiki/Energetick%C3%BD_a_pr%C5%AFmyslov%C3%BD_holding" title="Energetický a průmyslový holding">EPH</a> in a manner that avoids taxpayer involvement.  Instead, liabilities covering decommissioning and land rehabilitation could be paid by EPH directly into a foundation, perhaps run by the public company <a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lausitzer_und_Mitteldeutsche_Bergbau-Verwaltungsgesellschaft" class="extiw" title="de:Lausitzer und Mitteldeutsche Bergbau-Verwaltungsgesellschaft">LMBV</a>.  The study calculates the necessary provisions at €2.6<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion.<sup id="cite_ref-ieefa-2016_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ieefa-2016-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wynn-and-julve-2016_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wynn-and-julve-2016-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2016 the German utility <a href="/wiki/Evonik_Industries#Energy_Business_Area" title="Evonik Industries">STEAG</a> announced it will be decommissioning five coal-fired generating units in <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saarland" title="Saarland">Saarland</a> due to low wholesale electricity prices.<sup id="cite_ref-clew-2016a_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clew-2016a-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-handelsblatt-2016_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-handelsblatt-2016-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A coal phase-out for Germany is implied in Germany's <a href="/wiki/German_Climate_Action_Plan_2050" title="German Climate Action Plan 2050">Climate Action Plan 2050</a>, environment minister <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Hendricks_(politician)" title="Barbara Hendricks (politician)">Barbara Hendricks</a> said in an interview on 21<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>November 2016.  "If you read the Climate Action Plan carefully, you will find that the exit from coal-fired power generation is the immanent consequence of the energy sector target.<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... By 2030<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... half of the coal-fired power production must have ended, compared to 2014", she said.<sup id="cite_ref-clew-2016b_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clew-2016b-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-goetze-and-schwarz-2016_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-goetze-and-schwarz-2016-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Plans to cut down the ancient <a href="/wiki/Hambach_Forest" title="Hambach Forest">Hambach Forest</a> to extend the <a href="/wiki/Hambach_open_pit_mine" class="mw-redirect" title="Hambach open pit mine">Hambach open pit mine</a> in 2018 have resulted in massive protests.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 22 September 2016 the Dutch parliament voted for a 55% cut in CO<sub>2</sub> emissions by 2030, a move which would require the closure of the country's five coal-fired power plants.  The vote is not binding on the government however.<sup id="cite_ref-neslen=2016_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neslen=2016-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sweden">Sweden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sweden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sweden is constructing hydrogen based pilot steel plant to replace coke and coal usage in steel production.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Once this technology is commercialized with the <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_production" title="Hydrogen production">hydrogen generated</a> from renewable energy sources (<a href="/wiki/Biogas" title="Biogas">biogas</a> or electricity), the carbon foot print of steel production would reduce drastically.<sup id="cite_ref-cf_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cf-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:India_Coal_Production.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/India_Coal_Production.png/220px-India_Coal_Production.png" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/India_Coal_Production.png/330px-India_Coal_Production.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/India_Coal_Production.png/440px-India_Coal_Production.png 2x" data-file-width="2150" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:India_Coal_Production.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coal Production in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, with a 1959-2020 axis (appears to end at 2012)</div></div></div>
<p>India is the third largest consumer of coal in the world. India's federal energy minister is planning to stop importing thermal coal by 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
The annual report of India's Power Ministry has a plan to grow power by about 80GW as part of their 11th 5-year plan, and 79% of that growth will be in fossil fuel–fired power plants, primarily coal.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>  India plans four new "ultra mega" coal-fired power plants as part of that growth, each 4000MW in capacity. As of 2015 there are six nuclear reactors under construction. In the first half of 2016, the amount of coal-fired generating capacity in pre-construction planning in India fell by 40,000 MW, according to results released by the Global Coal Plant Tracker.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In June 2016, India's Ministry of Power stated that no further power plants would be required in the next three years, and "any thermal power plant that has yet to begin construction should back off."<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In cement production, carbon neutral biomass is being used to replace coal for reducing carbon foot print drastically.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cf_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cf-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In October 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Helen_Clark" title="Helen Clark">Clark</a> <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Labour_Party" title="New Zealand Labour Party">Labour</a> government introduced a 10<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>year moratorium on new fossil fuel thermal power generation.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>  The ban was limited to state-owned utilities, although an extension to the private sector was considered.  The <a href="/wiki/Fifth_National_Government_of_New_Zealand" title="Fifth National Government of New Zealand">new government</a> under MP <a href="/wiki/John_Key" title="John Key">John Key</a> (<a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_National_Party" title="New Zealand National Party">NZNP</a>) <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_general_election,_2008" title="New Zealand general election, 2008">elected in November 2008</a> repealed this legislation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In 2014, almost 80 per cent of the electricity produced in <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> was from <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_energy" title="Sustainable energy">sustainable energy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> 
On 6 August 2015, <a href="/wiki/Genesis_Energy_Limited" title="Genesis Energy Limited">Genesis Energy Limited</a> announced that it would close its two last <a href="/wiki/Fossil-fuel_power_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil-fuel power station">coal-fired power stations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa">South Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: South Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of 2007, South Africa's power sector is the 8th highest global emitter of CO<sub>2</sub>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> In 2005/2006, 77% of South Africa's energy demand was directly met by coal,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> and when current projects come online, this ratio will increase in the near term.
</p><p>There are no plans to phase out coal-fired power plants in South Africa, and indeed, the country is investing in building massive amounts of new coal-fired capacity to meet power demands, as well as modernizing the existing coal-fired plants to meet environmental requirements.
</p><p>On April 6, 2010, the World Bank approved a $3.75B loan to South Africa to support the construction of the world's 4th largest coal-fired plant, at Medupi.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
The proposed World Bank loan includes a relatively small amount - $260 million  - for wind and solar power.
</p><p>Rated at 4800MW, <a href="/wiki/Medupi_Power_Station" title="Medupi Power Station">Medupi Power Station</a> would join other mammoth coal-fired power plants already in operation in the country, namely <a href="/wiki/Kendal_Power_Station" title="Kendal Power Station">Kendal Power Station</a> (4100MW), <a href="/wiki/Majuba_Power_Station" title="Majuba Power Station">Majuba Power Station</a> (4100), and <a href="/wiki/Matimba_Power_Station" title="Matimba Power Station">Matimba Power Station</a> (4000), as well as a similar-capacity <a href="/wiki/Kusile_Power_Station" title="Kusile Power Station">Kusile Power Station</a>, at 4800MW, currently under construction.  Kusile is expected to come online in stages, starting in 2012, while Medupi is expected to first come online in 2013, with full capacity available by 2017.  These schedules are provisional, and may change.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Since 2008, South Africa's government started funding <a href="/wiki/Solar_water_heating" title="Solar water heating">solar water heating</a> installations. As of January 2016, there have been 400 000 domestic installations in total, with free-of-charge installation of low-pressure solar water heaters for low-cost homes or low-income households which have access to the electricity grid, while other installations are subsidised.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ed_Miliband" title="Ed Miliband">Ed Miliband</a> (<a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Energy_and_Climate_Change" title="Secretary of State for Energy and Climate Change">energy secretary</a> from 3 October 2008 – 11 May 2010) announced that no new coal-fired power stations will be built in Britain from 2009 onwards unless they capture and bury at least 25% of greenhouse gases immediately and 100% by 2025 although at the time this was a statement of intent rather than something he was able to enforce.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Chris_Huhne" title="Chris Huhne">Chris Huhne</a> (energy secretary from 12 May 2010 – 5 February 2012) has confirmed that the legislation required to allow his office to enforce <a href="/wiki/Emission_standard#UK" title="Emission standard">emissions standards</a> are proceeding.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The UK is also subject to the EU's <a href="/wiki/Large_Combustion_Plant_Directive" title="Large Combustion Plant Directive">Large Combustion Plant Directive</a> covering non-CO2 emissions which is expected to bring many older plants to a close over the next few years as they are too expensive to upgrade.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Amber_Rudd" title="Amber Rudd">Amber Rudd</a> (energy secretary from 11 May 2015) announced on 18 November 2015 that all coal-fired power stations would close by 2025. This will not be a complete phase out of fossil fuels because new gas-fired power stations will replace them.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The closure of the last coal power station in March 2016 ended coal-fired <a href="/wiki/Energy_policy_of_Scotland" title="Energy policy of Scotland">power production in Scotland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2017, fossil fuels provided 81 percent of the energy consumed in the United States, down from 86 percent in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
