<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Estimated_Effect_of_Carbon_Tax_in_US.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Estimated_Effect_of_Carbon_Tax_in_US.png/220px-Estimated_Effect_of_Carbon_Tax_in_US.png" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Estimated_Effect_of_Carbon_Tax_in_US.png/330px-Estimated_Effect_of_Carbon_Tax_in_US.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Estimated_Effect_of_Carbon_Tax_in_US.png/440px-Estimated_Effect_of_Carbon_Tax_in_US.png 2x" data-file-width="1322" data-file-height="888" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Estimated_Effect_of_Carbon_Tax_in_US.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Estimated effect of a <a href="/wiki/Carbon_tax" title="Carbon tax">carbon tax</a> on sources of United States electrical generation (US Energy Information Administration)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Total_Energy_1949-2011.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/US_Total_Energy_1949-2011.png/220px-US_Total_Energy_1949-2011.png" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/US_Total_Energy_1949-2011.png/330px-US_Total_Energy_1949-2011.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/US_Total_Energy_1949-2011.png/440px-US_Total_Energy_1949-2011.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Total_Energy_1949-2011.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Total energy consumption in the US by source: comparing fossil fuels with nuclear and renewable energy.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Electricity_Fossil_Fuels_vs_Others.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/US_Electricity_Fossil_Fuels_vs_Others.png/220px-US_Electricity_Fossil_Fuels_vs_Others.png" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/US_Electricity_Fossil_Fuels_vs_Others.png/330px-US_Electricity_Fossil_Fuels_vs_Others.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/US_Electricity_Fossil_Fuels_vs_Others.png/440px-US_Electricity_Fossil_Fuels_vs_Others.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Electricity_Fossil_Fuels_vs_Others.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>US electrical generation: fossil fuels vs. nuclear and renewable energy</div></div></div>
<p>In 2007, 154 new coal-fired plants were on the drawing board in 42 states.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> By 2012, that had dropped to 15, mostly due to new rules limiting mercury emissions, and limiting carbon emissions to 1,000 pounds of CO<sub>2</sub> per megawatt-hour of electricity produced.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2013, US Secretary of Energy <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Moniz" title="Ernest Moniz">Ernest Moniz</a> outlined Obama administration policy on fossil fuels:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>In the last four years, we’ve more than doubled renewable energy generation from wind and solar power.  However, coal and other fossil fuels still provide 80 percent of our energy, 70 percent of our electricity, and will be a major part of our energy future for decades.  That’s why any serious effort to protect our kids from the worst effects of climate change must also include developing, demonstrating and deploying the technologies to use our abundant fossil fuel resources as cleanly as possible.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>Then-US Energy Secretary <a href="/wiki/Steven_Chu" title="Steven Chu">Steven Chu</a> and researchers for the US <a href="/wiki/National_Renewable_Energy_Laboratory" title="National Renewable Energy Laboratory">National Renewable Energy Laboratory</a> have noted that greater electrical generation by non-<a href="/wiki/Dispatchable_generation" title="Dispatchable generation">dispatchable</a> renewables, such as wind and solar, will also increase the need for flexible natural gas-powered generators, to supply electricity during those times when solar and wind power are unavailable.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Gas-powered generators have the ability to ramp up and down quickly to meet changing loads.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the US, many of the fossil fuel phase-out initiatives have taken place at the state or local levels.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:California_Electricity_Sources_2010.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/California_Electricity_Sources_2010.png/220px-California_Electricity_Sources_2010.png" width="220" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/California_Electricity_Sources_2010.png/330px-California_Electricity_Sources_2010.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/California_Electricity_Sources_2010.png/440px-California_Electricity_Sources_2010.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="850" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:California_Electricity_Sources_2010.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>California electricity generation by source, 2010 (data from US EIA)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maine_Electricity_Source.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Maine_Electricity_Source.png/220px-Maine_Electricity_Source.png" width="220" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Maine_Electricity_Source.png/330px-Maine_Electricity_Source.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Maine_Electricity_Source.png/440px-Maine_Electricity_Source.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="950" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maine_Electricity_Source.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sources of electricity generated in Maine. 2010 (US EIA)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Texas_Electricity_Source.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Texas_Electricity_Source.png/220px-Texas_Electricity_Source.png" width="220" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Texas_Electricity_Source.png/330px-Texas_Electricity_Source.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Texas_Electricity_Source.png/440px-Texas_Electricity_Source.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="950" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Texas_Electricity_Source.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sources of electricity generated in Texas, 2010 (US EIA)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Washington_state_Electricity_Source.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Washington_state_Electricity_Source.png/220px-Washington_state_Electricity_Source.png" width="220" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Washington_state_Electricity_Source.png/330px-Washington_state_Electricity_Source.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Washington_state_Electricity_Source.png/440px-Washington_state_Electricity_Source.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="950" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Washington_state_Electricity_Source.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sources of electricity generation in Washington state, 2010 (US EIA)</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="California">California</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: California">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>'s SB 1368 created the first governmental moratorium on new coal plants in the United States. The law was signed in September 2006 by <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> Governor <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schwarzenegger" title="Arnold Schwarzenegger">Arnold Schwarzenegger</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> took effect for investor-owned utilities in January 2007, and took effect for publicly owned utilities in August 2007. SB 1368 applied to long-term investments (five years or more) by California utilities, whether in-state or out-of-state. It set the standard for greenhouse gas emissions at 1,100 pounds of carbon dioxide per megawatt-hour, equal to the emissions of a combined-cycle natural gas plant. This standard created a de facto moratorium on new coal, since it could not be met without carbon capture and sequestration.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Maine">Maine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Maine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On April 15, 2008, <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a> Governor <a href="/wiki/John_E._Baldacci" class="mw-redirect" title="John E. Baldacci">John E. Baldacci</a> signed LD 2126, "An Act To Minimize Carbon Dioxide Emissions from New Coal-Powered Industrial and Electrical Generating Facilities in the State." The law, which was sponsored by Rep. W. Bruce MacDonald (D-<a href="/wiki/Boothbay,_Maine" title="Boothbay, Maine">Boothbay</a>), requires the Board of Environmental Protection to develop greenhouse gas emission standards for coal gasification facilities. It also puts a moratorium in place on building any new coal gasification facilities until the standards are developed.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Oregon">Oregon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Oregon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In early March 2016, Oregon lawmakers approved a plan to stop paying for out-of-state coal plants by 2030 and require a 50 percent renewable energy standard by 2040.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Environmental groups such as the <a href="/wiki/American_Wind_Energy_Association" title="American Wind Energy Association">American Wind Energy Association</a> and leading Democrats praised the bill.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Texas">Texas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Texas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2006 a coalition of <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> groups organized a campaign in favor of a statewide moratorium on new coal-fired power plants. The campaign culminated in a "Stop the Coal Rush" mobilization, including rallying and lobbying, at the state capital in  <a href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas" title="Austin, Texas">Austin</a> on February 11 and 12th, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Over 40 citizen groups supported the mobilization.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January, 2007, A resolution calling for a 180-day moratorium on new pulverized coal plants was filed in the Texas Legislature by State Rep. <a href="/wiki/Charles_%22Doc%22_Anderson" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles &quot;Doc&quot; Anderson">Charles "Doc" Anderson</a> (R-Waco) as House Concurrent Resolution 43.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> The resolution was left pending in committee.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> On December 4, 2007, Rep. Anderson announced his support for two proposed  <a href="/wiki/Integrated_gasification_combined_cycle" title="Integrated gasification combined cycle">integrated gasification combined cycle</a> (IGCC) coal plants proposed by <a href="/wiki/Luminant" title="Luminant">Luminant</a> (formerly TXU).<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Washington_state">Washington state</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Washington state">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Washington_(U.S._state)" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington (U.S. state)">Washington</a> has followed the same approach as California, prohibiting coal plants whose emissions would exceed those of natural gas plants. Substitute Senate Bill 6001 (SSB 6001), signed on May 3, 2007, by Governor <a href="/wiki/Christine_Gregoire" title="Christine Gregoire">Christine Gregoire</a>, enacted the standard.<sup id="cite_ref-whitmanpioneer.com_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whitmanpioneer.com-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> As a result of SSB 6001, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20090716184525/http://www.energy-northwest.com/generation/igcc/index.php">Pacific Mountain Energy Center</a> in Kalama was rejected by the state. However, a new plant proposal, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.wallulaenergy.com/">Wallula Energy Resource Center</a>, shows the limits of the "natural gas equivalency" approach as a means of prohibiting new coal plants. The proposed plant would meet the standard set by SSB 6001 by capturing and sequestering a portion (65 percent, according to a plant spokesman) of its carbon.<sup id="cite_ref-whitmanpioneer.com_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whitmanpioneer.com-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Utility_action_in_the_US">Utility action in the US</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Utility action in the US">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Progress_Energy_Carolinas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Progress Energy Carolinas (page does not exist)">Progress Energy Carolinas</a><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> announced on June 1, 2007, that it was beginning a two-year moratorium on proposals for new coal-fired power plants while it undertook more aggressive efficiency and conservation programs. The company added, "Additional reductions in future electricity demand growth through energy efficiency could push the need for new power plants farther into the future."<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Public_Service_of_Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Public Service of Colorado (page does not exist)">Public Service of Colorado</a><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> concluded in its November 2007 Resource Plan: "In sum, in light of the now likely regulation of CO<sub>2</sub> emissions in the future due to broader interest in climate change issues, the increased costs of constructing new coal facilities, and the increased risk of timely permitting to meet planned in-service dates, Public Service does not believe it would not be prudent to consider at this time any proposals for new coal plants that do not include CO<sub>2</sub> capture and sequestration.<sup id="cite_ref-burned_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burned-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Xcel_Energy" title="Xcel Energy">Xcel Energy</a> noted in its 2007 Resource Plan that "given the likelihood of future carbon regulation, we have only modeled a future coal-based resource option that includes carbon capture and storage."<sup id="cite_ref-burned_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burned-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Minnesota_Power_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Minnesota Power Company (page does not exist)">Minnesota Power Company</a><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> announced in December 2007 that it would not consider a new coal resource without a carbon solution.<sup id="cite_ref-burned_120-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burned-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Avista_Utilities" class="mw-redirect" title="Avista Utilities">Avista Utilities</a><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> announced that it does not anticipate pursuing coal-fired power plants in the foreseeable future.<sup id="cite_ref-burned_120-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burned-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/NorthWestern_Energy" class="mw-redirect" title="NorthWestern Energy">NorthWestern Energy</a><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> announced on December 17, 2007, that it planned to double its wind power capacity over the next seven years and steer away from new baseload coal plants. The plans are detailed in the company's 2007 Montana Electric Supply Resource Plan.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/California_Energy_Commission" title="California Energy Commission">California Energy Commission</a> (CEC) has initiated its review of two 53.4-megawatt solar thermal power plants that will each include a 40-megawatt biomass power plant to supplement the solar power.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Japan, the world's third-largest economy, made a major move to use more fossil fuels in 2012, when the nation shut down nuclear reactors following the Fukishima accident. Nuclear, which had supplied 30 percent of Japanese electricity from 1987 to 2011, supplied only 2 percent in 2012 (hydropower supplied 8 percent). Nuclear electricity was replaced with electricity from petroleum, coal, and liquified natural gas. As a result, electricity generation from fossil fuels rose to 90 percent in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2017, the Japanese government announced plans to build 45 new coal-fired power plants in the next ten years, largely to replace expensive electricity from petroleum power plants.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_opinion">Public opinion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Public opinion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="rquote pullquote floatright" role="presentation" style="border-collapse:collapse; border-style:none; float:right; margin:0.5em 0.75em; width:33%;">

<tbody><tr style="text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:&#39;Times New Roman&#39;,serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">“
</td>
<td style="padding:0 10px;">Those corporations that continue to invest in new fossil fuel exploration, new fossil fuel exploitation, are really in flagrant breach of their fiduciary duty because the science is abundantly clear that this is something we can no longer do.
</td>
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:&#39;Times New Roman&#39;,serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; text-align:right; vertical-align:bottom; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">”
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td class="rquotecite" colspan="3" style="padding-top:10px; font-size:smaller; line-height:normal; text-align:right;"><cite>—&#160;<a href="/wiki/Christiana_Figueres" title="Christiana Figueres">Christiana Figueres</a>,&#32;executive secretary of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Framework_Convention_on_Climate_Change" title="United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change">United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change</a><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opinion_polls">Opinion polls</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Opinion polls">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Opinion_research">Opinion research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Opinion research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In October, 2007, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.civilsocietyinstitute.org/">Civil Society Institute</a> released the results of a poll of 1,003 U.S. citizens conducted by Opinion Research Corporation.
</p><p>The authors of the poll reported:
"75 percent of Americans—including 65 percent of Republicans, 83 percent of Democrats and 76 percent of Independents—would 'support a five-year moratorium on new coal-fired power plants in the United States if there was stepped-up investment in clean, safe renewable energy—such as wind and solar—and improved home energy-efficiency standards.' Women (80 percent) were more likely than men (70 percent) to support this idea. Support also was higher among college graduates (78 percent) than among those who did not graduate from high school (68 percent)."<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The exact question posed by the survey was as follows:
More than half of power plant-generated electricity comes from coal. Experts say that power plants are responsible for about 40 percent of U.S. carbon dioxide pollution linked to global warming. There are plans to build more than 150 new coal-fired power plants over the next several years. Would you support a five-year moratorium on new coal-fired power plants in the United States if there was stepped-up investment in clean, safe and renewable energy—such as wind and solar—and improved home energy-efficiency standards? Would you say definitely yes, probably yes, probably no, definitely no, or don't know.
</p><p>The results were as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>30% "definitely yes"</li>
<li>45% "probably yes"</li>
<li>13% "probably no"</li>
<li>8% "definitely no"</li>
<li>4% "don't know"</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gallup">Gallup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Gallup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2013, the Gallup organization determined that 41% of Americans wanted less emphasis placed on coal energy, versus 31% who wanted more. Large majorities wanted more emphasis placed on solar (76%), wind (71%), and natural gas (65%).<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="ABC_News.2FWashington_Post"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="ABC_News/Washington_Post">ABC News/Washington Post</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: ABC News/Washington Post">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A 2009 ABC/Washington Post poll found 52% of Americans favored more coal mining (33% strongly favored), while 45% opposed (27% strongly opposed). The most support was for wind and solar, which were favored by 91% (79% strongly favored).<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="CLEAN_call_to_action">CLEAN call to action</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: CLEAN call to action">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In October, 2007, fifteen groups led by <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://theclean.org/">Citizens Lead for Energy Action Now</a> (CLEAN) called for a five-year moratorium on new coal-fired power plants, with no exception for plants sequestering carbon. The groups included Save Our Cumberland Mountains (Tennessee); Ohio Valley Environmental Council (West Virginia); Cook Inlet Keeper (Alaska); Christians for the Mountains (West Virginia); Coal River Mountain Watch (West Virginia); Kentuckians for the Commonwealth (Kentucky); Civil Society Institute (Massachusetts); Clean Power Now (Massachusetts); Indigenous Environmental Network (Minnesota); Castle Mountain Coalition (Alaska); Citizens Action Coalition (Indiana); Appalachian Center for the Economy &amp; the Environment (West Virginia); Appalachian Voices (NC); and Rhode Island Wind Alliance (Rhode Island).<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_Defense_Fund">Environmental Defense Fund</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Environmental Defense Fund">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The US-based <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Defense_Fund" title="Environmental Defense Fund">Environmental Defense Fund</a> (EDF) has taken a stand in favor of natural gas production and <a href="/wiki/Hydraulic_fracturing" title="Hydraulic fracturing">hydraulic fracturing</a>, while pressing for stricter environmental controls on gas drilling, as a feasible way to replace coal.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The organization has funded studies jointly with the petroleum industry on the environmental effects of natural gas production. The organization sees natural gas as a way to quickly replace coal, and that natural gas in time will be replaced by renewable energy.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> The policy has been criticized by some environmentalists.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> EDF counsel and blogger Mark Brownstein answered:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Demand for natural gas is not going away, and neither is hydraulic fracturing.  We must be clear-eyed about this, and fight to protect public health and the environment from unacceptable impacts.  We must also work hard to put policies in place that ensure that natural gas serves as an enabler of renewable power generation, not an impediment to it.  We fear that those who oppose all natural gas production everywhere are, in effect, making it harder for the U.S. economy to wean itself from dirty coal.</p><div class="templatequotecite">—&#8201;<cite>Mark Brownstein, EDF council<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_groups_supporting_a_coal_moratorium">Other groups supporting a coal moratorium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Other groups supporting a coal moratorium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/1Sky" title="1Sky">1Sky</a><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Co-op_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Co-op America">Co-op America</a><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Energy_Action_Coalition" class="mw-redirect" title="Energy Action Coalition">Energy Action Coalition</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_anti-nuclear_groups_in_the_United_States#Sierra_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="List of anti-nuclear groups in the United States">Kansas Sierra Club</a><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Environmental_groups_and_resources_serving_K%E2%80%9312_schools#Energy_Action_Coalition" title="Environmental groups and resources serving K–12 schools">Lead for Energy Action Now (CLEAN)</a><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rainforest_Action_Network" title="Rainforest Action Network">Rainforest Action Network</a><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rising_Tide_North_America" title="Rising Tide North America">Rising Tide</a> Australia<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sierra_Club" title="Sierra Club">Sierra Club</a><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SixDegrees.org" title="SixDegrees.org">SixDegrees.org</a><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Step_It_Up_2007#Step_It_Up" class="mw-redirect" title="Step It Up 2007">Step It Up! 2007</a><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shareholder_resolutions_in_favor_of_a_coal_moratorium">Shareholder resolutions in favor of a coal moratorium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Shareholder resolutions in favor of a coal moratorium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.trilliuminvest.com/">Trillium Asset Management</a>, a social investment management company, submitted the resolution <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://trilliuminvest.com/resolutions/moritorium-on-coal-financing/">"Moratorium on Coal Financing"</a> to Bank of America in the 2007–2008 shareholder resolution season. The resolution concluded:</li></ul>
<blockquote>
<p>RESOLVED: Shareholders request that BOA's board of directors amend its GHG emissions policies to observe a moratorium on all financing, investment and further involvement in activities that support MTR coal mining or the construction of new coal-burning power plants that emit carbon dioxide.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prominent_individuals_supporting_a_coal_moratorium">Prominent individuals supporting a coal moratorium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Prominent individuals supporting a coal moratorium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>US politician <a href="/wiki/Albert_Gore,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Albert Gore, Jr.">Al Gore</a> stated:<sup id="cite_ref-nichols-2008_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nichols-2008-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>If you're a young person looking at the future of this planet and looking at what is being done right now, and not done, I believe we have reached the stage where it is time for <a href="/wiki/Civil_disobedience" title="Civil disobedience">civil disobedience</a> to prevent the construction of new coal plants that do not have carbon capture and sequestration.
</p></blockquote>
<ul><li>Banker and financier <a href="/wiki/Tom_Sanzillo" class="mw-redirect" title="Tom Sanzillo">Tom Sanzillo</a>, currently First Deputy Comptroller for the state of New York, called for a moratorium on new coal plants in the state of Iowa. Citing slow growth in electricity demand and better alternative sources of energy, Sanzillo said, "It's not only good public policy, it's great economics."<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prominent_individuals_supporting_a_coal_phase-out">Prominent individuals supporting a coal phase-out</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Prominent individuals supporting a coal phase-out">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Eric_Schmidt" title="Eric Schmidt">Eric Schmidt</a>, CEO of Google, called for replacing all <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a> with renewable sources of energy in twenty years.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mayors_supporting_a_coal_moratorium">Mayors supporting a coal moratorium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Mayors supporting a coal moratorium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 13 October 2007, Pocatello, Idaho, mayor Roger Chase told other mayors from across the state attending an Association of Idaho Cities legislative committee that he favored a moratorium no new coal plants in the state.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 1 June 2007, Park City, Utah, mayor Dana Wilson wrote a letter to <a href="/wiki/Warren_Buffett" title="Warren Buffett">Warren Buffett</a> expressing the city's opposition to three coal plants proposed by Rocky Mountain Power.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2007, Salt Lake City mayor <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Anderson" title="Rocky Anderson">Rocky Anderson</a> expressed his support for a coal moratorium at a rally organized by the Step It Up! campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2007, Charlottesville, VA, mayor Dave Norris blogged in favor of a moratorium on new coal-fired power plants.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> On 19 December 2007, Charlottesville passed the Charlottesville Clean Energy Resolution putting the city on record as supporting a moratorium.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_governments_supporting_a_coal_moratorium">Local governments supporting a coal moratorium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Local governments supporting a coal moratorium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January, 2008, Black Hawk County (Iowa) Health Board recommended that the state adopt a moratorium on new coal-fired power plants until it enacts tougher air pollution standards.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_Sources_of_Energy">Alternative Sources of Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Alternative Sources of Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Alternative_energy" title="Alternative energy">Alternative energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Energy_transition" title="Energy transition">Energy transition</a>, and <a href="/wiki/100%25_renewable_energy" title="100% renewable energy">100% renewable energy</a></div><p><a href="/wiki/Alternative_energy" title="Alternative energy">Alternative energy</a> refers to any source of energy that can substitute the role of fossil fuels. <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">Renewable energy</a>, or energy that is harnessed from <a href="/wiki/Renewable_resource" title="Renewable resource">renewable sources</a>, is an alternative energy. However, alternative energy can refer to non renewable sources as well, like <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear energy</a>. Between the alternative sources of energy are: <a href="/wiki/Solar_energy" title="Solar energy">solar energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectricity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marine_energy" title="Marine energy">marine energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_energy" title="Geothermal energy">geothermal energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethanol" title="Ethanol">ethanol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_economy" title="Hydrogen economy">Hydrogen</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">Energy efficiency</a> is complementary to the use of alternative energy sources, when phasing-out fossil fuels.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Renewable_energy">Renewable energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Renewable energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bp_world_energy_consumption_2016.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Bp_world_energy_consumption_2016.gif/220px-Bp_world_energy_consumption_2016.gif" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Bp_world_energy_consumption_2016.gif/330px-Bp_world_energy_consumption_2016.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Bp_world_energy_consumption_2016.gif/440px-Bp_world_energy_consumption_2016.gif 2x" data-file-width="482" data-file-height="290" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bp_world_energy_consumption_2016.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The worldwide growth of renewable energy is shown by the green line<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Renewable energy is <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">energy</a> that comes from resources which are naturally replenished such as <a href="/wiki/Sunlight" title="Sunlight">sunlight</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wind" title="Wind">wind</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rain" title="Rain">rain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tidal_energy" class="mw-redirect" title="Tidal energy">tides</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wave_power" title="Wave power">waves</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_energy" title="Geothermal energy">geothermal heat</a>. As of 2014, 19% of global final energy consumption comes from <a href="/wiki/Renewable_resource" title="Renewable resource">renewable resources</a>, with 9% of all energy from traditional <a href="/wiki/Biomass" title="Biomass">biomass</a>, mainly used for <a href="/wiki/Heating" class="mw-redirect" title="Heating">heating</a>, 1% from biofuels, 4% from <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectricity</a> and 4% from biomass, geothermal or solar heat . Popular renewables (wind, solar, geothermal and biomass for power) accounted for another 1.4% and are growing rapidly.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> While renewable energy supplies are growing and have displaced coal in some regions, the amount of coal burned in 2021, is expected to be the same as it was in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydroelectricity">Hydroelectricity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Hydroelectricity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chief_Joseph_Dam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Chief_Joseph_Dam.jpg/220px-Chief_Joseph_Dam.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Chief_Joseph_Dam.jpg/330px-Chief_Joseph_Dam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Chief_Joseph_Dam.jpg/440px-Chief_Joseph_Dam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="993" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chief_Joseph_Dam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Chief_Joseph_Dam" title="Chief Joseph Dam">Chief Joseph Dam</a> near <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport,_Washington" title="Bridgeport, Washington">Bridgeport, Washington</a>, USA, is a major run-of-the-river station without a sizeable reservoir.</div></div></div>
<p>In 2015 <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectric energy</a> generated 16.6% of the worlds total electricity and 70% of all renewable electricity.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> In Europe and North America environmental concerns around land flooded by large <a href="/wiki/Reservoir" title="Reservoir">reservoirs</a> ended 30 years of dam construction in the 1990s. Since then large dams and reservoirs continue to be built in countries like China, Brazil and India. <a href="/wiki/Run-of-the-river_hydroelectricity" title="Run-of-the-river hydroelectricity">Run-of-the-river hydroelectricity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Small_hydro" title="Small hydro">small hydro</a> have become popular alternatives to conventional dams that may create reservoirs in environmentally sensitive areas.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wind_power">Wind power</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Wind power">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wind_farm" title="Wind farm">Wind farm</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Turbiny_wiatrowe_w_Szwecji,_2011_ubt.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Turbiny_wiatrowe_w_Szwecji%2C_2011_ubt.JPG/220px-Turbiny_wiatrowe_w_Szwecji%2C_2011_ubt.JPG" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Turbiny_wiatrowe_w_Szwecji%2C_2011_ubt.JPG/330px-Turbiny_wiatrowe_w_Szwecji%2C_2011_ubt.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Turbiny_wiatrowe_w_Szwecji%2C_2011_ubt.JPG/440px-Turbiny_wiatrowe_w_Szwecji%2C_2011_ubt.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="1729" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Turbiny_wiatrowe_w_Szwecji,_2011_ubt.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lillgrund_Wind_Farm" title="Lillgrund Wind Farm">Lillgrund Wind Farm</a> in Sweden</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Windpark_Estinnes_20juli2010_kort_voor_voltooiing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Windpark_Estinnes_20juli2010_kort_voor_voltooiing.jpg/220px-Windpark_Estinnes_20juli2010_kort_voor_voltooiing.jpg" width="220" height="47" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Windpark_Estinnes_20juli2010_kort_voor_voltooiing.jpg/330px-Windpark_Estinnes_20juli2010_kort_voor_voltooiing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Windpark_Estinnes_20juli2010_kort_voor_voltooiing.jpg/440px-Windpark_Estinnes_20juli2010_kort_voor_voltooiing.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2785" data-file-height="593" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Windpark_Estinnes_20juli2010_kort_voor_voltooiing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>First wind farm consisting of 7,5 MW Enercon E-126 turbines, <a href="/wiki/Estinnes" title="Estinnes">Estinnes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, 20 July 2010, two months before completion; note the 2-part blades.</div></div></div>
<p>A wind farm is a group of <a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine" title="Wind turbine">wind turbines</a> in the same location used to produce electric power. A large wind farm may consist of several hundred individual wind turbines, and cover an extended area of hundreds of square miles, but the land between the turbines may be used for agricultural or other purposes. A wind farm may also be located offshore.
</p><p>Wind power has grown dramatically since 2005 and by 2015 supplied almost 1% of global energy consumption.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Many of the largest operational onshore wind farms are located in the United States and China. The <a href="/wiki/Gansu_Wind_Farm" title="Gansu Wind Farm">Gansu Wind Farm</a> in China has over 5,000 MW installed with a goal of 20,000 MW by 2020. China has several other "wind power bases" of similar size. The <a href="/wiki/Alta_Wind_Energy_Center" title="Alta Wind Energy Center">Alta Wind Energy Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, United States is the largest onshore wind farm outside of China, with a capacity of 1020 <a href="/wiki/Megawatt" class="mw-redirect" title="Megawatt">MW</a> of power.<sup id="cite_ref-terragen_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-terragen-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> As of February 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Walney_Wind_Farm" title="Walney Wind Farm">Walney Wind Farm</a> in the United Kingdom is the largest offshore wind farm in the world at 367 <a href="/wiki/Megawatt" class="mw-redirect" title="Megawatt">MW</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Thanet_Offshore_Wind_Project" class="mw-redirect" title="Thanet Offshore Wind Project">Thanet Offshore Wind Project</a> (300 MW), also in the United Kingdom. As of February 2012, the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A2nt%C3%A2nele-Cogealac_Wind_Farm" title="Fântânele-Cogealac Wind Farm">Fântânele-Cogealac Wind Farm</a> in Romania is the largest onshore wind farm in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> at 600 <a href="/wiki/Megawatt" class="mw-redirect" title="Megawatt">MW</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cez_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cez-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are many large wind farms under construction and these include <a href="/wiki/Sinus_Holding_Wind_Farm" title="Sinus Holding Wind Farm">Sinus Holding Wind Farm</a> (700 MW), <a href="/wiki/Anholt_Offshore_Wind_Farm" title="Anholt Offshore Wind Farm">Anholt Offshore Wind Farm</a> (400 MW), <a href="/wiki/BARD_Offshore_1" title="BARD Offshore 1">BARD Offshore 1</a> (400 MW), <a href="/wiki/Clyde_Wind_Farm" title="Clyde Wind Farm">Clyde Wind Farm</a> (350 MW), <a href="/wiki/Greater_Gabbard_wind_farm" title="Greater Gabbard wind farm">Greater Gabbard wind farm</a> (500 MW), <a href="/wiki/Lincs_Wind_Farm" title="Lincs Wind Farm">Lincs Wind Farm</a> (270 MW), <a href="/wiki/London_Array" title="London Array">London Array</a> (1000 MW), <a href="/wiki/Lower_Snake_River_Wind_Project" title="Lower Snake River Wind Project">Lower Snake River Wind Project</a> (343 MW), <a href="/wiki/Macarthur_Wind_Farm" title="Macarthur Wind Farm">Macarthur Wind Farm</a> (420 MW), <a href="/wiki/Shepherds_Flat_Wind_Farm" title="Shepherds Flat Wind Farm">Shepherds Flat Wind Farm</a> (845 MW), and <a href="/wiki/Sheringham_Shoal_Offshore_Wind_Farm" title="Sheringham Shoal Offshore Wind Farm">Sheringham Shoal</a> (317 MW).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Wind_power_in_Denmark" title="Wind power in Denmark">Wind power in Denmark</a> produced the equivalent of 42.1% of total electricity consumption in 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-euractiv1_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-euractiv1-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-enet42_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-enet42-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> however, use of wind for heating is minor.<sup id="cite_ref-wittboil_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wittboil-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Solar">Solar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Solar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>By 2020 the solar contribution to global final energy consumption will exceed 1%.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Solar_photovoltaics">Solar photovoltaics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Solar photovoltaics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LieberoseSolarpark.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/LieberoseSolarpark.jpg/220px-LieberoseSolarpark.jpg" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/LieberoseSolarpark.jpg/330px-LieberoseSolarpark.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/LieberoseSolarpark.jpg/440px-LieberoseSolarpark.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="315" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LieberoseSolarpark.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 71.8 MW <a href="/wiki/Lieberose_Photovoltaic_Park" title="Lieberose Photovoltaic Park">Lieberose Photovoltaic Park</a> in Germany.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_photovoltaic_power_stations" title="List of photovoltaic power stations">List of photovoltaic power stations</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Solar_photovoltaic_cell" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar photovoltaic cell">Solar photovoltaic cells</a> convert sunlight into electricity and many solar <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic_power_station" title="Photovoltaic power station">photovoltaic power stations</a> have been built. The size of these stations has increased progressively over the last decade with frequent new capacity <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic_power_station#Noteworthy_solar_parks" title="Photovoltaic power station">records</a>.
</p><p>As of January 2013, the largest individual photovoltaic (PV) power plants in the world are <a href="/wiki/Agua_Caliente_Solar_Project" title="Agua Caliente Solar Project">Agua Caliente Solar Project</a>, (Arizona, over 247&#160;MW connected - to increase to 397&#160;MW), <a href="/wiki/Golmud_Solar_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Golmud Solar Park">Golmud Solar Park</a> (China, 200&#160;MW), <a href="/wiki/Mesquite_Solar_project" title="Mesquite Solar project">Mesquite Solar project</a> (Arizona, 150&#160;MW), <a href="/wiki/Neuhardenberg_Solar_Park" title="Neuhardenberg Solar Park">Neuhardenberg Solar Park</a> (Germany, 145&#160;MW), <a href="/wiki/Templin_Solar_Park" title="Templin Solar Park">Templin Solar Park</a> (Germany, 128&#160;MW), <a href="/wiki/Toul-Rosi%C3%A8res_Solar_Park" title="Toul-Rosières Solar Park">Toul-Rosières Solar Park</a> (France, 115&#160;MW), and <a href="/wiki/Perovo_Solar_Park" title="Perovo Solar Park">Perovo Solar Park</a> (Ukraine, 100&#160;MW). The <a href="/wiki/Charanka_Solar_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Charanka Solar Park">Charanka Solar Park</a> is a collection of solar power stations of which 214 MW were reported complete in April 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-Charanka_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charanka-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> on a 2000 <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">ha</a> site.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> It is part of <a href="/wiki/Gujarat_Solar_Park" title="Gujarat Solar Park">Gujarat Solar Park</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> a group of solar farms at various locations in the <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> state of India, with overall capacity of 702 MW.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> There are a total of 570 MW of solar parks in Golmud, with 500 MW more expected in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Many large plants are under construction. The <a href="/wiki/Desert_Sunlight_Solar_Farm" title="Desert Sunlight Solar Farm">Desert Sunlight Solar Farm</a> is a 550 MW <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a> plant under construction in <a href="/wiki/Riverside_County,_California" title="Riverside County, California">Riverside County, California</a>, that will use thin-film solar <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Photovoltaic">photovoltaic</a> modules made by <a href="/wiki/First_Solar" title="First Solar">First Solar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rew11_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rew11-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Topaz_Solar_Farm" title="Topaz Solar Farm">Topaz Solar Farm</a> is a 550 MW photovoltaic power plant, being built in <a href="/wiki/San_Luis_Obispo_County,_California" title="San Luis Obispo County, California">San Luis Obispo County, California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-re11_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-re11-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Blythe_Solar_Power_Project" class="mw-redirect" title="Blythe Solar Power Project">Blythe Solar Power Project</a> is a 500 MW photovoltaic station under construction in <a href="/wiki/Riverside_County,_California" title="Riverside County, California">Riverside County, California</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Agua_Caliente_Solar_Project" title="Agua Caliente Solar Project">Agua Caliente Solar Project</a> is a 290 megawatt photovoltaic solar generating facility being built in <a href="/wiki/Yuma_County,_Arizona" title="Yuma County, Arizona">Yuma County, Arizona</a>. The <a href="/wiki/California_Valley_Solar_Ranch" title="California Valley Solar Ranch">California Valley Solar Ranch</a> (CVSR) is a 250&#160;<a href="/wiki/Megawatt" class="mw-redirect" title="Megawatt">megawatt</a> (MW) <a href="/wiki/Solar_photovoltaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar photovoltaic">solar photovoltaic</a> <a href="/wiki/Power_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Power plant">power plant</a>, which is being built by <a href="/wiki/SunPower" title="SunPower">SunPower</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Carrizo_Plain" title="Carrizo Plain">Carrizo Plain</a>, northeast of <a href="/wiki/California_Valley,_California" title="California Valley, California">California Valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> The 230 MW <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_plants_in_the_Mojave_Desert#Antelope_Valley_Solar_Ranch" title="Solar power plants in the Mojave Desert">Antelope Valley Solar Ranch</a> is a <a href="/wiki/First_Solar" title="First Solar">First Solar</a> photovoltaic project which is under construction in the Antelope Valley area of the Western Mojave Desert, and due to be completed in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Many of these plants are integrated with agriculture and some use innovative tracking systems that follow the sun's daily path across the sky to generate more electricity than conventional fixed-mounted systems. Solar power plants have no fuel costs or emissions during operation.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Concentrated_solar_power">Concentrated solar power</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Concentrated solar power">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:12-05-08_AS1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/12-05-08_AS1.JPG/220px-12-05-08_AS1.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/12-05-08_AS1.JPG/330px-12-05-08_AS1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/12-05-08_AS1.JPG/440px-12-05-08_AS1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3504" data-file-height="2336" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:12-05-08_AS1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 150 MW <a href="/wiki/Andasol_solar_power_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Andasol solar power station">Andasol solar power station</a> is a commercial <a href="/wiki/Parabolic_trough" title="Parabolic trough">parabolic trough</a> <a href="/wiki/Solar_thermal" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar thermal">solar thermal</a> power plant, located in <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_in_Spain" title="Renewable energy in Spain">Spain</a>. The Andasol plant uses tanks of molten salt to store solar energy so that it can continue generating electricity even when the sun isn't shining.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Concentrated_solar_power" title="Concentrated solar power">Concentrated solar power</a></div>
<p>Concentrating Solar Power (CSP) systems use lenses or mirrors and tracking systems to focus a large area of sunlight into a small beam. The concentrated heat is then used as a heat source for a conventional power plant. A wide range of concentrating technologies exists; the most developed are the parabolic trough, the concentrating linear fresnel reflector, the Stirling dish and the solar power tower. Various techniques are used to track the Sun and focus light. In all of these systems a <a href="/wiki/Working_fluid" title="Working fluid">working fluid</a> is heated by the concentrated sunlight, and is then used for power generation or energy storage.<sup id="cite_ref-Martin_2005_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martin_2005-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biofuels">Biofuels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Biofuels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuel</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Biofuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Biofuels">Biofuels</a>, in the form of <a href="/wiki/Liquid_fuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Liquid fuels">liquid fuels</a> derived from plant materials, are entering the market. However, many of the biofuels that are currently being supplied have been criticised for their adverse impacts on the <a href="/wiki/Natural_environment" title="Natural environment">natural environment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food security</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Land_use" title="Land use">land use</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-roy_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roy-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sol_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sol-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biomass">Biomass</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Biomass">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Biomass" title="Biomass">Biomass</a> is <a href="/wiki/Biomaterial" title="Biomaterial">biological material</a> from living, or recently living organisms, most often referring to plants or plant-derived materials.<sup id="cite_ref-Biomass_Energy_Center_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Biomass_Energy_Center-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> As a <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_source" class="mw-redirect" title="Renewable energy source">renewable energy source</a>, biomass can either be used directly, or indirectly—once or converted into another type of energy product such as <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuel</a>. Biomass can be converted to energy in three ways: <i>thermal conversion</i>, <i>chemical conversion</i>, and <i>biochemical conversion</i>.
</p><p>Using biomass as a fuel produces <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a> in the form of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_monoxide" title="Carbon monoxide">carbon monoxide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>, <a href="/wiki/NOx" title="NOx">NOx</a> (nitrogen oxides), VOCs (<a href="/wiki/Volatile_organic_compound" title="Volatile organic compound">volatile organic compounds</a>), particulates and other pollutants at levels above those from traditional fuel sources such as <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> or <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>  in some cases (such as with indoor heating and cooking).<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> Utilization of wood biomass as a fuel can also produce fewer particulate and other pollutants than open burning as seen in wildfires or direct heat applications.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Black_carbon" title="Black carbon">Black carbon</a> – a pollutant created by combustion of fossil fuels, biofuels, and biomass – is possibly the second largest contributor to global warming.<sup id="cite_ref-starke-2009_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-starke-2009-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>56–57</span></sup> In 2009 a Swedish study of the giant brown haze that periodically covers large areas in South Asia determined that it had been principally produced by biomass burning, and to a lesser extent by fossil fuel burning.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Denmark" title="Energy in Denmark">Denmark</a> has increased the use of biomass and garbage,<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> and decreased the use of coal.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nuclear_energy">Nuclear energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Nuclear energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 2014 <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a> report identifies nuclear energy as one of the technologies that can  provide electricity with less than 5% of the lifecycle greenhouse gas emissions of coal power.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> There are more than 60 nuclear reactors shown as under construction in the list of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_by_country" title="Nuclear power by country">Nuclear power by country</a> with China leading at 23. Globally, more nuclear power reactors have closed than opened in recent years but overall capacity has increased.<sup id="cite_ref-econ13_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econ13-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> China has stated its plans to double nuclear generation by 2030. India also plans to greatly increase its nuclear power.
</p><p>Several countries have enacted laws to cease construction on new nuclear power stations. Several European countries have debated <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_phase-out" title="Nuclear power phase-out">nuclear phase-outs</a> and others have completely shut down some reactors. Three <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_accidents" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear accidents">nuclear accidents</a> have influenced the slowdown of nuclear power: the 1979 <a href="/wiki/Three_Mile_Island_accident" title="Three Mile Island accident">Three Mile Island accident</a> in the United States, the 1986 <a href="/wiki/Chernobyl_disaster" title="Chernobyl disaster">Chernobyl disaster</a> in the USSR, and the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Fukushima_nuclear_disaster" class="mw-redirect" title="Fukushima nuclear disaster">Fukushima nuclear disaster</a> in Japan. Following the March 2011 Fukushima nuclear disaster, Germany has permanently shut down eight of its 17 reactors and pledged to close the rest by the end of 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-Annika_Breidthardt_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Annika_Breidthardt-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> Italy voted overwhelmingly to keep their country non-nuclear.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> Switzerland and Spain have banned the construction of new reactors.<sup id="cite_ref-nweek11_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nweek11-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> Japan’s prime minister has called for a dramatic reduction in Japan’s reliance on nuclear power.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> Taiwan’s president did the same. <a href="/wiki/Shinz%C5%8D_Abe" title="Shinzō Abe">Shinzō Abe</a>, the new prime minister of Japan since December 2012, announced a plan to restart some of the 54 Japanese nuclear power plants and to continue some nuclear reactors under construction.
</p><p>As of 2016, countries such as <a href="/wiki/Anti-nuclear_movement_in_Australia" title="Anti-nuclear movement in Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anti-nuclear_movement_in_Austria" title="Anti-nuclear movement in Austria">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_energy_in_Denmark" title="Nuclear energy in Denmark">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_energy_in_Greece" title="Nuclear energy in Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_energy_in_Malaysia" title="Nuclear energy in Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand%27s_nuclear-free_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="New Zealand&#39;s nuclear-free zone">New Zealand</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_energy_in_Norway" title="Nuclear energy in Norway">Norway</a> have no nuclear power stations and remain opposed to nuclear power.<sup id="cite_ref-economist.com_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economist.com-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gl2011_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gl2011-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Anti-nuclear_movement_in_Germany" title="Anti-nuclear movement in Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anti-nuclear_movement_in_Spain" title="Anti-nuclear movement in Spain">Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anti-nuclear_movement_in_Switzerland" title="Anti-nuclear movement in Switzerland">Switzerland</a> are phasing-out their nuclear power.<sup id="cite_ref-econ13_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econ13-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gl2011_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gl2011-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-James_Kanter_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-James_Kanter-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_efficiency">Energy efficiency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Fossil_fuel_phase-out&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Energy efficiency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">Efficient energy use</a></div>
<p>Moving away from fossil fuels will require changes not only in the way energy is supplied, but in the way it is used, and reducing the amount of energy required to deliver various goods or services is essential. Opportunities for improvement on the demand side of the energy equation are as rich and diverse as those on the supply side, and often offer significant economic benefits.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A sustainable energy economy requires commitments to both renewables and efficiency.  Renewable energy and <a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">energy efficiency</a> are said to be the "twin pillars" of <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_energy" title="Sustainable energy">sustainable energy</a> policy. <a href="/wiki/American_Council_for_an_Energy-Efficient_Economy" title="American Council for an Energy-Efficient Economy">The American Council for an Energy-Efficient Economy</a> has explained that both resources must be developed in order to stabilize and reduce carbon dioxide emissions:<sup id="cite_ref-am_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-am-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<blockquote>
<p>Efficiency is essential to slowing the energy demand growth so that rising clean energy supplies can make deep cuts in fossil fuel use. If energy use grows too fast, renewable energy development will chase a receding target. Likewise, unless clean energy supplies come online rapidly, slowing demand growth will only begin to reduce total emissions; reducing the carbon content of energy sources is also needed.<sup id="cite_ref-am_205-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-am-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<p>The IEA has stated that renewable energy and energy efficiency policies are complementary tools for the development of a sustainable energy future, and should be developed together instead of being developed in isolation.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
